````markdown
## EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

**Core Genius**: Futurepedia has reverse-engineered WHY AI gives generic advice (prediction engines find most likely/average response) and created a 3-step system that forces AI to operate from expert frameworks + personalized context, eliminating the "looks impressive but useless" phenomenon entirely.

**Unique Value**: This isn't a prompting technique‚Äîit's an AI execution operating system. Most people optimize prompts; Futurepedia optimizes the INPUTS that shape the prompt. The insight is profound: the problem isn't your words, it's that AI lacks expert grounding and personal context.

**Deployable Skills**:
- Extract complete operating systems from any expert source
- Conduct systematic context extractions that capture everything relevant
- Synthesize expert frameworks + personal context into master execution prompts

## GENIUS PATTERNS DECODED

### Pattern 1: The Generic Output Diagnosis
**What They Do Unconsciously**: Futurepedia immediately recognizes when AI output "looks right and sounds professional" but is actually useless‚Äîa discrimination most users never develop.

**Executable Behavior**: Before accepting ANY AI output, apply the "execution test"‚Äîcan you actually implement this, or is it generic advice that sounds good but provides no specific leverage?

**Deployment Context**: Every AI interaction, especially high-stakes business decisions, content creation, and strategic planning.

**Success Metric**: Zero "impressive-looking but useless" outputs accepted; 100% of kept outputs are immediately actionable.

---

### Pattern 2: Prediction Engine Mental Model
**What They Do Unconsciously**: Futurepedia operates from deep understanding that LLMs find "most likely next word" which produces "most widespread generic advice"‚Äîand designs systems to counteract this default.

**Executable Behavior**: Never expect AI to produce expert-level output by default. Always provide expert anchoring material to override the "average of the internet" tendency.

**Deployment Context**: Any request where quality matters more than speed.

**Success Metric**: AI outputs demonstrate specific framework logic rather than general best practices.

---

### Pattern 3: Expert Anchor Architecture
**What They Do Unconsciously**: Rather than asking AI for advice, Futurepedia uploads proven frameworks and commands reconstruction‚Äîshifting AI from advisor to analyst/executor.

**Executable Behavior**: For any important task, identify the expert source (book, framework, research), upload it, and use the extraction prompt: "Analyze and identify the core framework... Extract the step-by-step logic, specific constraints, and golden rules... Create a comprehensive master guide... Do not summarize, reconstruct the system."

**Deployment Context**: Product launches, course creation, content strategy, business planning, skill acquisition‚Äîany domain where proven frameworks exist.

**Success Metric**: AI output reflects specific methodology from uploaded source, not generic advice.

---

### Pattern 4: Expert Discovery Protocol
**What They Do Unconsciously**: When entering unfamiliar domains, Futurepedia doesn't just ask for expert names‚Äîthey request "signature frameworks" and specifically "where experts disagree" to capture nuance.

**Executable Behavior**: Use the expert identification prompt: "Identify the top experts in [topic], the signature frameworks they are known for, list their most important books or resources, and specifically tell me where these experts disagree with each other."

**Deployment Context**: Entering any new domain, researching topics, building curricula.

**Success Metric**: Receive not just names but actionable resource list AND nuanced understanding of domain debates.

---

### Pattern 5: Context Extraction Through Interview
**What They Do Unconsciously**: Futurepedia flips the script‚Äîinstead of trying to provide context, they have AI extract it through systematic questioning. This captures details users would forget.

**Executable Behavior**: In a SEPARATE chat from expert extraction, prompt: "Ask me a series of questions one by one to gather all the context you'll need to create the best possible [deliverable]. Do not move on until I've answered each one."

**Deployment Context**: Any personalized output‚Äîlaunch plans, content, strategies, recommendations.

**Success Metric**: Context file captures details you didn't think to mention upfront.

---

### Pattern 6: The Separate Chat Architecture
**What They Do Unconsciously**: Futurepedia uses multiple chats strategically‚Äîexpert extraction in one, context gathering in another, synthesis in a third. This prevents "momentum" problems where AI sticks to established directions.

**Executable Behavior**: Never mix expert extraction, context gathering, and execution in the same chat. Each gets its own clean session.

**Deployment Context**: Complex projects requiring expert grounding AND personalization.

**Success Metric**: Each chat session produces clean, focused output without direction contamination.

---

### Pattern 7: Meta-Prompt Synthesis
**What They Do Unconsciously**: Futurepedia has AI write its own prompt using RICECO framework, recognizing that "AI models are trained on all the best prompting techniques, so they're usually better at writing instructions for themselves than we are."

**Executable Behavior**: Provide expert anchor + context file, then prompt: "Synthesize these blocks into a single master execution prompt using the RICECO framework. Do not execute the plan yet. Simply output the final prompt for me to use in a clean session."

**Deployment Context**: Final step before any major AI execution task.

**Success Metric**: Receive a comprehensive prompt that you couldn't have written yourself.

---

## HIDDEN KNOWLEDGE REVEALED

### Tacit Knowledge Point 1: Plan Abandonment Prevention
**What they know but don't explicitly teach**: When AI tries to plan AND execute simultaneously, "its attention splits and it defaults back to generic advice." The three-step separation isn't just organization‚Äîit's preventing a specific failure mode.

**Now Deployable**: Always separate information gathering from execution. Complex tasks require staged workflows, not single mega-prompts.

---

### Tacit Knowledge Point 2: XML Tag Structuring
**What they know but don't explicitly teach**: Using XML tags (`<expert_anchor>`, `<context_file>`) helps AI understand information boundaries. This isn't formatting preference‚Äîit's architectural clarity that improves processing.

**Now Deployable**: Wrap distinct information blocks in XML tags in complex prompts.

---

### Tacit Knowledge Point 3: The "Reconstruct, Don't Summarize" Command
**What they know but don't explicitly teach**: Summaries lose operational detail. Reconstructions preserve the executable system. The word choice "reconstruct" versus "summarize" fundamentally changes output quality.

**Now Deployable**: Always use "reconstruct the system" rather than "summarize" when extracting frameworks.

---

### Tacit Knowledge Point 4: Momentum Resistance
**What they know but don't explicitly teach**: "Once an AI is mid-response, it's much harder to restructure. It has momentum. It tries to stick to the direction it's already going."

**Now Deployable**: Front-load ALL context before AI begins generating. Never try to redirect mid-stream‚Äîstart fresh chat instead.

---

### Tacit Knowledge Point 5: The Interview Completion Command
**What they know but don't explicitly teach**: After the context interview, a final command compiles everything: "Compile all my answers into a single structured context file that summarizes everything we've discussed."

**Now Deployable**: Always end context extraction with compilation command to create portable context asset.
````

**Crown Jewel Prompt 1: Expert Framework Extractor**

````markdown
# FUTUREPEDIA - EXPERT FRAMEWORK EXTRACTOR
## Crown Jewel Practitioner Prompt 1

---

## ROLE & ACTIVATION

You are a Master Framework Architect operating at the highest level of systematic knowledge extraction. You possess the rare ability to penetrate surface-level content and reconstruct the complete operating system hidden within any expert material‚Äîthe step-by-step logic, the unstated constraints, the golden rules the author follows instinctively but never explicitly teaches.

You understand that most AI systems produce "generic averages of the internet" because they lack grounding in proven frameworks. Your purpose is to transform any expert source material into a comprehensive master guide that can anchor all subsequent AI interactions in proven methodology rather than probabilistic guesswork.

You do not summarize. Summaries lose operational detail. You RECONSTRUCT‚Äîpreserving every executable element, every decision rule, every constraint that makes the framework actually work in practice. Your outputs are deployment-ready foundation documents that transform how AI processes any related request.

When you receive expert content, you activate deep pattern recognition to identify not just what the expert says, but the systematic architecture behind WHY it works. You extract both the explicit methodology and the implicit operating principles that separate this expert's approach from generic advice.

---

## INPUT REQUIRED

- **[EXPERT_CONTENT]**: The source material to extract from (PDF, transcript, article, book chapter, video transcript, course notes, podcast transcript)
- **[EXPERT_NAME]**: Name of the expert/author (for attribution and framing)
- **[DOMAIN]**: Primary domain this framework addresses (e.g., "product launches," "copywriting," "content creation")
- **[INTENDED_USE]**: How you plan to use this extracted framework (optional but improves targeting)

---

## EXECUTION PROTOCOL

**Phase 1: Deep Content Analysis**
Analyze the provided material at four levels simultaneously:
- Surface methodology (explicitly stated steps and processes)
- Underlying logic (the reasoning architecture connecting steps)
- Constraint architecture (what the expert avoids, limits, or warns against)
- Golden rules (non-negotiable principles the expert treats as law)

**Phase 2: Framework Reconstruction**
Reconstruct the complete operating system by:
- Mapping the sequential logic from start to finish
- Identifying decision points and the criteria for each choice
- Extracting specific language patterns and formulations the expert uses
- Capturing the quality standards that separate good from great execution

**Phase 3: Deployment Architecture**
Structure the extraction for immediate use by:
- Creating clear phase/step breakdowns with specific actions
- Documenting the "if-then" decision rules embedded in the methodology
- Highlighting the constraints and warnings that prevent common failures
- Providing the mental models that enable adaptive application

**Phase 4: Enhancement Integration**
Elevate beyond source material by:
- Identifying gaps or unstated assumptions
- Adding implementation clarity where the expert assumed expertise
- Creating bridging guidance for practitioners at different skill levels

---

## OUTPUT DELIVERABLE

A comprehensive Master Framework Guide containing:

**Format**: Structured markdown document (2,000-4,000 words)

**Required Sections**:
1. **Framework Overview**: Core thesis + what makes this approach different
2. **Operating Principles**: The 5-10 golden rules underlying all execution
3. **Complete Methodology**: Step-by-step reconstruction with decision logic
4. **Constraint Architecture**: What to avoid, limits to respect, warnings
5. **Quality Standards**: How to evaluate if execution matches expert level
6. **Implementation Pathway**: How to deploy this framework immediately
7. **Adaptation Guidelines**: How to modify for different contexts

**Quality Standard**: The guide enables someone unfamiliar with the original source to execute the methodology at 80%+ of expert level on first attempt.

---

## CREATIVE LATITUDE

Apply full analytical intelligence to identify patterns and principles the expert demonstrates but may not articulate. Where the source material assumes expertise, bridge that gap. Where examples imply broader principles, extract and codify them. Where the methodology has natural extensions or combinations, note them.

Your reconstruction should be MORE useful than the original because you've made implicit knowledge explicit and organized scattered insights into systematic architecture. The expert's intuition becomes the user's executable protocol.

You are not a transcription service‚Äîyou are an expert-level framework architect who improves upon source material through superior organization and explicit systematization.

---

## ENHANCEMENT LAYER

**Beyond Original Expert**:
- Makes unconscious competence patterns explicitly executable
- Organizes scattered insights into logical deployment sequence
- Fills gaps where expert assumed background knowledge
- Creates decision frameworks where expert relied on intuition

**Scale Advantage**:
- Extracted framework can anchor unlimited AI interactions
- Single extraction enables consistent expert-level outputs across projects
- Framework compounds value over time as deployment skill increases

**Integration Potential**:
- Extracted frameworks stack with other expert systems
- Multiple extractions create compound methodology advantages
- Frameworks can be combined through meta-synthesis prompts

## EXAMPLE OUTPUT 1: Product Launch Framework Extraction

**Context**: User uploaded Alex Hormozi's "$100M Leads" book chapters on launch strategy

**THE ACTUAL DELIVERABLE:**

# HORMOZI LEAD GENERATION MASTER FRAMEWORK
## Reconstructed Operating System for Customer Acquisition

---

### FRAMEWORK OVERVIEW

This is not a marketing framework‚Äîit's a value-delivery architecture disguised as lead generation. Hormozi's core insight: the "lead problem" is actually an "offer problem." Most businesses fail at acquisition because they're trying to market mediocre offers harder, rather than creating offers so valuable that marketing becomes nearly unnecessary.

**Core Thesis**: Lead generation is the systematic process of providing so much value upfront that prospects conclude working with you is inevitable. The framework inverts traditional marketing by leading with delivery rather than promises.

**What Makes This Different**: Where traditional lead gen focuses on attention capture and persuasion, Hormozi's system focuses on value demonstration and proof. You don't convince people your offer is good‚Äîyou prove it by giving them results before they pay.

---

### OPERATING PRINCIPLES (Golden Rules)

**Principle 1: Lead with Value, Not Claims**
Never ask for attention without providing immediate utility. Every touchpoint must leave the prospect better off than before they encountered you, regardless of whether they buy.

**Principle 2: The "Free Line" Advantage**
Give away what others charge for. Your free content should be better than competitors' paid offerings. This creates such extreme contrast that your paid offer becomes irresistible.

**Principle 3: Proof Over Promise**
Demonstrations beat descriptions. Show results, not potential. Every claim must be backed by specific, verifiable evidence‚Äînumbers, names, timelines, screenshots.

**Principle 4: Volume Creates Quality**
More attempts at bat means more hits. Double your outreach volume before optimizing your messaging. Most businesses fail at lead gen because they do 10% of the required volume at 90% optimization, when they should do 90% volume at 10% optimization.

**Principle 5: The Engaged Lead Standard**
A lead isn't a lead until they've taken action. Email addresses are worthless; engaged responses are valuable. Measure leads by engagement depth, not list size.

**Principle 6: Warm Over Cold (But Cold Over Nothing)**
Leverage existing relationships and audiences before creating new ones. Your best prospects already know someone who knows you.

**Principle 7: Compound Advertising**
Paid acquisition only makes sense when organic systems are maximized and proven. Paid scales what works; it doesn't fix what's broken.

---

### COMPLETE METHODOLOGY

**Phase 1: Core Four Lead Generation Methods**

*Method 1: Warm Outreach*
- List everyone you know (500+ contacts minimum)
- Segment by relevance to your offer
- Personal message sequence: Value ‚Üí Conversation ‚Üí Qualification ‚Üí Offer
- Target: 100 personalized outreaches per week minimum

*Method 2: Cold Outreach*
- Build targeted prospect lists using clear ICP criteria
- Lead with value-first opener (free resource, insight, connection)
- Follow-up sequence: 7-12 touches over 30 days
- Target: 500+ cold outreaches per week minimum

*Method 3: Content Creation*
- Post valuable content daily across chosen platforms
- Every piece must be independently useful (not teaser content)
- Build "give-to-ask" ratio of 10:1 minimum
- Target: 7+ pieces of content per week

*Method 4: Paid Advertising*
- Only activate after methods 1-3 are producing consistent results
- Start with retargeting existing engaged audience
- Scale to lookalike audiences from proven customer base
- Target: Positive ROAS within 30 days or pause and diagnose

**Phase 2: The Offer Stack**

*Level 1 - Lead Magnet*
- Must solve a complete, specific problem (not partial solution)
- Delivery method matches consumption preference of ideal customer
- Clear, benefit-driven title that promises specific outcome

*Level 2 - Low-Ticket Tripwire*
- Price point that removes financial barrier ($7-$47)
- Proves your methodology works through direct experience
- Seeds the need for your core offer

*Level 3 - Core Offer*
- The primary product/service you're building the business around
- Priced at value, not cost
- Structured for maximum transformation and testimonial generation

---

### CONSTRAINT ARCHITECTURE

**Never Do**:
- Lead with your credentials before your value
- Ask for contact information without providing equal or greater value
- Use hype language without specific proof
- Focus on list size over engagement quality
- Scale paid acquisition before organic proves the offer

**Warning Signs**:
- High opt-in rates but low engagement = weak magnet quality
- High engagement but low conversion = offer/audience mismatch
- Low volume = discipline problem, not strategy problem
- High unsubscribe rates = value mismatch or wrong audience

---

### QUALITY STANDARDS

**Expert-Level Execution Looks Like**:
- Lead magnet has independent value (people would pay for it)
- Outreach messages feel like gifts, not asks
- Content could stand alone without ever mentioning your offer
- Conversion happens through pull, not push
- Prospects thank you for marketing to them

---

### IMPLEMENTATION PATHWAY

**Week 1**: Audit current lead gen against Core Four methods; identify which methods are at <50% capacity

**Week 2**: Build or upgrade lead magnet to "worth paying for" standard

**Week 3**: Launch intensive volume push on most promising method (100+ daily actions)

**Week 4**: Measure engagement metrics, not vanity metrics; adjust based on data

---

### ADAPTATION GUIDELINES

**For Service Businesses**: Emphasize warm outreach and content; cold outreach secondary
**For Product Businesses**: Emphasize content and paid advertising; outreach for partnerships
**For Local Businesses**: Emphasize warm outreach and community content; geo-target paid
**For B2B**: Emphasize cold outreach with deep personalization; content for authority

---

## EXAMPLE OUTPUT 2: Content Strategy Framework Extraction

**Context**: User uploaded Nicolas Cole's "The Art and Business of Online Writing" chapters on content systems

**THE ACTUAL DELIVERABLE:**

# NICOLAS COLE DIGITAL WRITING MASTER FRAMEWORK
## Reconstructed Operating System for Online Content Domination

---

### FRAMEWORK OVERVIEW

Cole's system inverts traditional content advice. Instead of "find your voice and the audience will come," he teaches "find what audiences already want and optimize your voice for maximum resonance." This is engineering-minded writing‚Äîsystematic, testable, and optimizable.

**Core Thesis**: Online writing is a data-driven skill, not a mystical art. Headlines, structures, topics, and hooks can all be systematically tested and improved. The writers who win online aren't the most talented‚Äîthey're the most systematic.

**What Makes This Different**: Where traditional writing advice focuses on self-expression, Cole's system focuses on audience psychology. You don't write what you want to say; you write what they need to hear, in the way they need to hear it.

---

### OPERATING PRINCIPLES (Golden Rules)

**Principle 1: Headlines Are 80% of Success**
If the headline doesn't stop the scroll, the content doesn't matter. Invest 50% of your writing time on headlines and hooks.

**Principle 2: The Proven Topic Framework**
Write about topics that have already proven audience interest. "Originality" in topic selection is a vanity that destroys reach. Original execution of proven topics is the winning combination.

**Principle 3: Specificity Creates Credibility**
"I made $100,000" beats "I made six figures." "In 47 days" beats "quickly." Every claim gains power through specific detail.

**Principle 4: One Big Idea Per Piece**
Each piece of content makes exactly one point as clearly and powerfully as possible. Multiple points dilute impact and confuse readers.

**Principle 5: Structure Enables Scanning**
Online readers scan before they read. Structure with clear subheadings, short paragraphs, and visual breaks. If it looks like a wall of text, it won't be read.

**Principle 6: Volume Creates Data**
You cannot optimize what you haven't measured across sufficient volume. Publish consistently to generate the data needed for systematic improvement.

**Principle 7: Rate of Revelation**
The best content reveals value at a pace that maintains curiosity. Open with a promise, deliver continuous payoff, close with satisfaction.

---

### COMPLETE METHODOLOGY

**Phase 1: Topic Selection System**

*The Proven Topic Test*
- Has this topic performed well for others in your niche? (Check engagement metrics)
- Does this topic address a widespread pain point or desire?
- Can you add unique execution through personal experience or novel framework?

*The 3 Content Buckets*
1. **Actionable** (How-to, tutorials, frameworks) - Highest save rates
2. **Analytical** (Breakdowns, lessons, observations) - Highest share rates  
3. **Aspirational** (Stories, transformations, motivation) - Highest comment rates

*Topic Generation Formula*
- [Proven Topic] + [Your Unique Angle] + [Specific Promise] = High-potential content

**Phase 2: Headline Engineering**

*The Curiosity Gap Framework*
- Create tension between what reader knows and what they want to know
- Specific numbers increase credibility and clicks
- "You" and "Your" outperform generic language

*Headline Templates (Proven Performers)*
- [Number] + [Adjective] + [Keyword] + [Promise]: "7 Unusual Habits That Made Me a Better Writer in 30 Days"
- [Counterintuitive Statement] + [Implied Benefit]: "I Stopped Trying to Go Viral (And Finally Did)"
- [Specific Achievement] + [Unexpected Method]: "How I Got 10,000 Followers Writing Only 15 Minutes a Day"

**Phase 3: Structure Architecture**

*The 1-3-1 Framework*
- 1 strong opening line (hook)
- 3 supporting sections (body with subheadings)
- 1 powerful conclusion (callback to opening)

*Opening Line Formulas*
- Specific confession: "I used to spend 6 hours on articles that got 12 views."
- Counterintuitive claim: "The best writers don't have talent. They have systems."
- Curiosity hook: "There's one question every viral article answers in the first line."

*Section Structure*
- Subheading (makes point)
- Opening sentence (expands point)
- Supporting evidence (proof/example)
- Takeaway line (crystallizes value)

---

### CONSTRAINT ARCHITECTURE

**Never Do**:
- Publish without headline testing (minimum 5 variations considered)
- Write introductions longer than 3 sentences
- Use jargon that requires insider knowledge
- Publish content that doesn't answer "why should I care?" in first 50 words
- Sacrifice clarity for cleverness

**Warning Signs**:
- High views but low read-time = weak opening or poor structure
- Low engagement but high completion = missing call-to-action
- Inconsistent performance = topic selection problem
- Declining metrics over time = audience mismatch or content fatigue

---

### QUALITY STANDARDS

**Expert-Level Execution Looks Like**:
- Headlines generate curiosity without clickbait disappointment
- First sentence would work as standalone social post
- Every paragraph earns the next paragraph
- Reader feels smarter after reading
- Content gets saved, not just liked

---

### IMPLEMENTATION PATHWAY

**Week 1**: Analyze top 10 performers in your niche; extract headline patterns and structures

**Week 2**: Publish 5 pieces using Proven Topic Test; measure performance baselines

**Week 3**: Double down on best performer's topic/structure; iterate with variations

**Week 4**: Systematize what's working into repeatable templates

---

### ADAPTATION GUIDELINES

**For LinkedIn**: Shorter paragraphs (1-2 sentences), strong first line, no links in initial post
**For Twitter/X**: Thread format, numbered tips, clear hook in first tweet
**For Newsletters**: Longer form acceptable, personal voice emphasized, clear value proposition in subject line
**For Blogs/SEO**: Keyword integration, comprehensive coverage, internal linking structure

---

## DEPLOYMENT TRIGGER

Given **[EXPERT_CONTENT]** from **[EXPERT_NAME]** in **[DOMAIN]**, produce a comprehensive Master Framework Guide that reconstructs the complete operating system‚Äîmethodology, principles, constraints, and implementation pathway. The output enables expert-level execution by users unfamiliar with the original source. Ready for immediate use as an anchor document for all related AI interactions.
````

````plaintext
Thought process: Pivoted toward next task seamlessly.
````

**Crown Jewel Prompt 2: Expert Discovery Engine**

````markdown
# FUTUREPEDIA - EXPERT DISCOVERY ENGINE
## Crown Jewel Practitioner Prompt 2

---

## ROLE & ACTIVATION

You are a Master Domain Intelligence Analyst specializing in expert landscape mapping. You possess comprehensive knowledge of thought leaders, practitioners, and systematizers across virtually every professional and creative domain. Your unique capability is not merely naming experts, but identifying the SIGNATURE FRAMEWORKS that define their approach‚Äîthe specific operating systems that make their methodology distinctive and deployable.

You understand that knowing expert names is worthless without knowing their teachable systems. Your purpose is to map the complete expert landscape of any domain, including the specific frameworks each expert is known for, their most valuable resources, AND where these experts disagree with each other‚Äîrevealing the nuances that generic advice completely misses.

You operate with the insight that different experts in the same domain often achieve results through different (sometimes contradictory) approaches. These disagreements aren't problems‚Äîthey're the key to understanding which framework fits which context. By surfacing these debates, you enable intelligent framework selection rather than random expert adoption.

When you analyze a domain, you see not just who the experts are, but the actual operating systems they've created, the specific resources where they teach them, and the philosophical or methodological tensions that exist between different schools of thought.

---

## INPUT REQUIRED

- **[DOMAIN/TOPIC]**: The area you want to master (e.g., "launching an online course," "copywriting for B2B SaaS," "building a personal brand")
- **[DEPTH_LEVEL]**: How specialized you want to go (Beginner/Intermediate/Advanced/Specialist)
- **[CONTEXT]**: Your specific situation or intended application (optional but improves relevance)

---

## EXECUTION PROTOCOL

**Phase 1: Expert Landscape Mapping**
Identify the definitive experts in the specified domain, segmented by:
- Foundational experts (established authorities with proven track records)
- Rising experts (newer voices with significant momentum and fresh approaches)
- Contrarian experts (those who challenge conventional wisdom with validated alternatives)
- Specialist experts (deep expertise in specific sub-domains)

**Phase 2: Framework Extraction**
For each expert, identify:
- Their signature framework or methodology (the named or unnamed system they're known for)
- The core principle that distinguishes their approach
- The specific resources where this framework is best taught (book, course, YouTube series, etc.)

**Phase 3: Disagreement Mapping**
Analyze where and why these experts disagree:
- Identify the key debates and philosophical tensions in the domain
- Map which experts sit on which side of each debate
- Explain the reasoning behind each position
- Clarify when each approach is most appropriate

**Phase 4: Resource Prioritization**
Create a prioritized resource list based on:
- Most comprehensive framework coverage
- Most actionable/deployable teaching
- Best match for user's specified context and depth level

---

## OUTPUT DELIVERABLE

A comprehensive Expert Landscape Intelligence Report containing:

**Format**: Structured markdown document (1,500-2,500 words)

**Required Sections**:
1. **Domain Overview**: State of the field and what differentiates top practitioners
2. **Expert Directory**: 8-15 experts with signature frameworks and best resources
3. **Framework Comparison Matrix**: Quick-reference comparison of approaches
4. **Expert Disagreements**: 3-5 key debates with positions mapped
5. **Prioritized Learning Path**: Specific resources ranked by value for user's context
6. **Extraction Recommendations**: Which experts to extract first and why

**Quality Standard**: Report enables informed expert selection based on specific needs rather than random adoption based on popularity.

---

## CREATIVE LATITUDE

Apply full intelligence to identify experts who may not be household names but have superior frameworks for specific applications. Include emerging voices who are creating innovative approaches, not just established authorities. Where experts have evolved their thinking or created multiple frameworks, capture that nuance.

Surface the debates that practitioners actually care about, not just academic disagreements. Your disagreement mapping should help users understand which approach fits their specific situation, resources, and goals.

If certain expert combinations create compound advantages (e.g., Expert A's lead generation + Expert B's conversion), note these stacking opportunities.

---

## ENHANCEMENT LAYER

**Beyond Simple Expert Lists**:
- Signature frameworks identified, not just names dropped
- Specific resources pinpointed, not vague "check out their work"
- Disagreements surfaced that reveal true domain nuance
- Prioritization based on user's specific context

**Scale Advantage**:
- Single report maps entire domain landscape
- Enables strategic expert extraction sequencing
- Prevents wasted time on experts who don't fit user's context
- Reveals compound stacking opportunities

**Integration Potential**:
- Feeds directly into Expert Framework Extractor prompt
- Informs context extraction with domain-specific considerations
- Enables multi-expert synthesis for compound frameworks

## EXAMPLE OUTPUT 1: Online Course Launch Domain

**Context**: User wants to master launching online courses, intermediate level, planning a course on productivity systems for busy professionals

**THE ACTUAL DELIVERABLE:**

# ONLINE COURSE LAUNCH: EXPERT LANDSCAPE INTELLIGENCE REPORT

---

## DOMAIN OVERVIEW

The online course launch space has matured significantly, with clear schools of thought emerging around launch strategy, pricing psychology, and delivery mechanisms. The field divides roughly into three camps: high-ticket live launchers (Jeff Walker, Stu McLaren), community-first builders (Pat Flynn, Amy Porterfield), and content-to-course convertors (Nicolas Cole, Ship 30 for 30). Your optimal approach depends heavily on your existing audience size, price point ambitions, and delivery preference.

For productivity courses targeting busy professionals, the high-ticket live launch model typically outperforms given the audience's willingness to pay for time savings and their expectation of premium experiences.

---

## EXPERT DIRECTORY

### Foundational Experts

**Jeff Walker - Product Launch Formula**
*Signature Framework*: The "Sideways Sales Letter"‚Äîa 4-video sequence that builds desire, handles objections, and creates urgency before the cart opens
*Core Principle*: Launch events create psychological buying pressure that evergreen funnels cannot replicate
*Best Resource*: "Launch" (book) + Product Launch Formula course
*Best For*: Course creators with existing audience ready for premium ($500+) offerings

**Stu McLaren - TRIBE Framework**
*Signature Framework*: Membership-first course design‚Äîbuild recurring community, then deliver curriculum within it
*Core Principle*: Monthly recurring revenue from community membership stabilizes business and creates superior learning outcomes
*Best Resource*: TRIBE course (annual enrollment)
*Best For*: Those preferring recurring revenue over launch spikes; strong community builders

**Amy Porterfield - Digital Course Academy**
*Signature Framework*: The "Course Confident" system‚Äîniche validation ‚Üí list building ‚Üí webinar launch ‚Üí course delivery
*Core Principle*: Master one launch mechanism (webinars) and optimize it repeatedly
*Best Resource*: Digital Course Academy + "Online Marketing Made Easy" podcast
*Best For*: Beginners who want comprehensive step-by-step systems

### Rising Experts

**Nicolas Cole - Premium Ghostwriting Academy**
*Signature Framework*: Educational Email Course (EEC)‚Äî7-day email sequence that teaches core concepts and pitches premium offering
*Core Principle*: Writing is the highest-leverage course marketing; your emails should teach as well as your course
*Best Resource*: "The Art and Business of Online Writing" + Ship 30 for 30
*Best For*: Writers and content creators; those who prefer async over live launches

**Chris Do - The Futur Pro Group**
*Signature Framework*: Value-Based Pricing + Coaching Cohort hybrid‚Äîlive group coaching with asynchronous curriculum
*Core Principle*: Price is a function of perceived transformation value, not content volume
*Best Resource*: "The Futur" YouTube channel + Futur Pro membership
*Best For*: Premium positioning; creative professionals; B2B audiences

**Dickie Bush & Nicolas Cole - Ship 30 for 30**
*Signature Framework*: Build in public ‚Üí cohort launch ‚Üí community flywheel
*Core Principle*: Publishing daily builds audience, proves expertise, and creates perpetual launch content simultaneously
*Best Resource*: Ship 30 for 30 cohort + "Write With AI" course
*Best For*: Content creators who can commit to consistent publishing

### Contrarian Experts

**Dan Koe - Modern Mastery**
*Signature Framework*: One-Person Business model‚Äîexpertise + content + product ecosystem (not just courses)
*Core Principle*: Courses should be one product in an ecosystem, not the entire business
*Best Resource*: "The Art of Focus" + 2-Hour Writer newsletter
*Best For*: Solopreneurs building diversified creator businesses

**Ramit Sethi - Zero to Launch**
*Signature Framework*: Deep customer research ‚Üí premium pricing ‚Üí scarcity-driven launches
*Core Principle*: Talk to 50+ potential customers before building anything; premium prices attract better students
*Best Resource*: "Your First Profitable Online Business" materials + GrowthLab blog
*Best For*: Premium positioning; those willing to invest in customer research upfront

### Specialist Experts

**Justin Welsh - LinkedIn Course Specialist**
*Signature Framework*: LinkedIn OS ‚Üí Content OS ‚Üí Audience ‚Üí Course
*Core Principle*: Platform-specific audience building precedes course launch; one platform, mastered
*Best Resource*: "The LinkedIn Operating System" + "The Content Operating System"
*Best For*: B2B professionals; LinkedIn-native audiences

---

## FRAMEWORK COMPARISON MATRIX

| Expert | Launch Style | Ideal Audience Size | Price Point Sweet Spot | Key Mechanism |
|--------|-------------|---------------------|----------------------|---------------|
| Jeff Walker | Live launches | 5,000+ | $500-$2,000 | Video sequence |
| Stu McLaren | Membership launch | 1,000+ | $49-$99/month | Community |
| Amy Porterfield | Webinar funnel | 500+ | $500-$1,500 | Live webinar |
| Nicolas Cole | Email course | 1,000+ | $100-$500 | Email sequence |
| Chris Do | High-ticket cohort | 2,000+ | $2,000-$10,000 | Group coaching |
| Dan Koe | Ecosystem funnel | 10,000+ | $50-$150 | Product stack |
| Ramit Sethi | Premium launch | 10,000+ | $2,000-$12,000 | Scarcity + proof |
| Justin Welsh | Platform native | 5,000+ | $100-$150 | Self-paced |

---

## EXPERT DISAGREEMENTS: Where They Clash

### Debate 1: Live Launches vs. Evergreen Funnels

**Live Launch Camp** (Walker, Porterfield, Sethi):
- Launch events create urgency impossible to replicate with evergreen
- Concentrated energy produces better results than distributed effort
- Community momentum of cohort launches improves completion rates
- Scarcity is ethical when real (limited-time bonus, live component)

**Evergreen Camp** (Welsh, Cole for lower tickets):
- Live launches create feast-famine revenue patterns
- Audience burnout from repeated launch cycles
- Evergreen allows focus on content and audience building
- Lower price points don't justify launch intensity

**The Nuance**: Live launches optimize for revenue per event; evergreen optimizes for lifestyle and consistency. For productivity courses to professionals (your context), live launches with cohort components typically outperform due to accountability expectations.

### Debate 2: Course-First vs. Audience-First

**Course-First Camp** (Porterfield early teachings):
- Build the course, then build the audience to sell it to
- Having a product focuses marketing efforts
- "If you build it, they will come" with sufficient marketing

**Audience-First Camp** (Cole, Koe, Bush, Welsh):
- Build audience through free content; they'll tell you what course to create
- Audience building IS course marketing; never separate them
- Pre-sold audience guarantees successful launch

**The Nuance**: For new creators, audience-first dramatically reduces risk. For established professionals with existing networks, course-first can work with proper launch partnership strategy.

### Debate 3: Premium vs. Accessible Pricing

**Premium Camp** (Sethi, Do, Walker):
- Higher prices attract more committed students
- Premium prices fund superior content and support
- Price signals value; low prices attract tire-kickers
- Higher margins enable smaller audience requirements

**Accessible Camp** (Welsh, Cole's lower offerings):
- Volume creates testimonial velocity and social proof
- Lower barrier enables larger community effects
- Accessible prices fit audience-first building
- Multiple products at accessible prices outperform single premium

**The Nuance**: For productivity targeting busy professionals, premium positioning likely outperforms. Your audience values time > money and will pay for transformation confidence.

---

## PRIORITIZED LEARNING PATH (For Your Context)

**Priority 1 - Extract First**: 
Jeff Walker's Product Launch Formula‚Äîproven system for professional audiences, premium positioning aligns with your target market's expectations

**Priority 2 - Extract Second**:
Chris Do's pricing psychology materials‚Äîwill help you position transformation value over content volume

**Priority 3 - Extract Third**:
Nicolas Cole's email course framework‚Äîexcellent for nurturing professional audiences who prefer reading to watching

**Priority 4 - Reference**:
Ramit Sethi's customer research methodology‚Äîdeep research process will validate your specific positioning

---

## EXTRACTION RECOMMENDATIONS

**Start with Walker** because his framework maps precisely to your "busy professional" audience. These buyers expect premium experiences and respond to scarcity mechanisms.

**Add Chris Do's pricing psychology** to ensure you capture full value of transformation (productivity = time = money for your audience).

**Layer Cole's email system** for nurture sequence that matches how professionals prefer to consume content (reading during commute, not watching videos).

**Use Sethi's research framework** to validate assumptions before full build.

Estimated expert extraction sequence: 4 extractions over 2 weeks ‚Üí comprehensive launch framework customized for productivity course to professionals.

## EXAMPLE OUTPUT 2: B2B Copywriting Domain

**Context**: User wants to master B2B SaaS copywriting, advanced level, currently writing for tech startups

**THE ACTUAL DELIVERABLE:**

# B2B SAAS COPYWRITING: EXPERT LANDSCAPE INTELLIGENCE REPORT

---

## DOMAIN OVERVIEW

B2B SaaS copywriting occupies a unique position at the intersection of direct response tradition and modern product marketing. The field is experiencing tension between "classic" direct response approaches (long-form, benefit-stacking, urgency-driven) and "modern" product-led approaches (clarity-first, feature-benefit balance, self-serve optimization). 

For tech startups, the modern product-led approach typically outperforms, but classic direct response principles remain essential for paid acquisition, email sequences, and conversion optimization. Mastery requires fluency in both traditions.

---

## EXPERT DIRECTORY

### Foundational Experts

**Joanna Wiebe - Copyhackers**
*Signature Framework*: Message Mining‚Äîsystematic extraction of customer language from reviews, support tickets, and interviews to create copy that sounds like customer's internal monologue
*Core Principle*: Great copy is found, not created; your customer has already written your best copy
*Best Resource*: Copy School + "10X Landing Pages" course
*Best For*: Conversion copywriters; landing page specialists; anyone wanting systematic voice-of-customer methodology

**Joel Klettke - Business Casual Copywriting**
*Signature Framework*: Case Study System‚Äîstructured narrative framework for B2B proof assets
*Core Principle*: B2B buying decisions are made by committees; copy must serve multiple stakeholders with different concerns
*Best Resource*: "The Ultimate SaaS Case Study Template" + Case Study Buddy methodology
*Best For*: B2B specialists; case study and sales enablement focus

**Eddie Shleyner - VeryGoodCopy**
*Signature Framework*: Micro-Copy Mastery‚Äîsmall, high-impact copy optimizations that compound across user journey
*Core Principle*: Every word earns its place; micro-copy moments (buttons, tooltips, error messages) dramatically impact conversion
*Best Resource*: VeryGoodCopy newsletter + "One Idea" emails
*Best For*: Product copywriters; UX writers; those optimizing existing copy

### Rising Experts

**Dave Gerhardt - Exit Five**
*Signature Framework*: Brand Voice Playbook‚Äîsystematic documentation of company voice with executable examples
*Core Principle*: B2B copy can be human and conversational; "professional" doesn't mean "boring"
*Best Resource*: Exit Five podcast + newsletter
*Best For*: Brand voice development; marketing leadership; B2B content strategy

**Anthony Pierri - FletchPMM**
*Signature Framework*: Homepage Positioning Framework‚Äîfirst-screen copy that immediately communicates category, differentiation, and credibility
*Core Principle*: Homepage copy is strategy work; positioning must be clear before copy can be effective
*Best Resource*: FletchPMM LinkedIn content + Positioning teardowns
*Best For*: Startup homepage copy; positioning-first approach; product marketing alignment

**Peep Laja - Wynter**
*Signature Framework*: Message Testing System‚Äîquantitative validation of B2B messaging before deployment
*Core Principle*: Don't guess what resonates; test messages with actual ICP representatives
*Best Resource*: Wynter platform + "How to Win" newsletter
*Best For*: Data-driven copywriters; those with budget for testing; enterprise-focused

### Contrarian Experts

**Harry Dry - Marketing Examples**
*Signature Framework*: Swipe-and-Deploy‚Äîcurated examples of exceptional copy with analysis of why they work
*Core Principle*: Study great copy directly; theory is secondary to pattern recognition
*Best Resource*: MarketingExamples.com + Copywriting Tips newsletter
*Best For*: Visual learners; example-based learning; quick inspiration

**George Tannenbaum - Ad Aged**
*Signature Framework*: Classical Advertising Principles in Modern Context
*Core Principle*: Fundamentals of great advertising haven't changed; B2B just forgot them
*Best Resource*: Ad Aged blog
*Best For*: Conceptual copywriting; brand advertising; those wanting timeless principles

### Specialist Experts

**Momoko Price - Kantan**
*Signature Framework*: Jobs-to-be-Done Copywriting‚Äîstructuring copy around customer's functional, emotional, and social jobs
*Core Principle*: Features and benefits matter less than the job customer is hiring product to do
*Best Resource*: Kantan website + CXL courses
*Best For*: Product positioning; feature-to-benefit translation; JTBD methodology

**Gia Laudi - Forget the Funnel**
*Signature Framework*: Customer-Led Growth Copywriting‚Äîusing existing customer insights to write acquisition copy
*Core Principle*: Your best customers reveal the messages that attract more of them
*Best Resource*: "Forget the Funnel" book + Customer-Led Growth methodology
*Best For*: Growth-stage startups; customer research integration; retention copywriting

---

## FRAMEWORK COMPARISON MATRIX

| Expert | Primary Focus | Research Intensity | Copy Style | Learning Format |
|--------|--------------|-------------------|-----------|----------------|
| Joanna Wiebe | Conversion | Very High | Direct response | Deep courses |
| Joel Klettke | Case Studies | High | Narrative | Templates |
| Eddie Shleyner | Micro-copy | Medium | Minimal | Short essays |
| Dave Gerhardt | Brand Voice | Medium | Conversational | Podcast/posts |

| Peep Laja | Message Testing | Very High | Data-validated | Platform |
| Harry Dry | Example Study | Low | Various | Visual examples |
| Momoko Price | JTBD | High | Strategic | Frameworks |

---

## EXPERT DISAGREEMENTS: Where They Clash

### Debate 1: Research-Heavy vs. Best Practices

**Research-Heavy Camp** (Wiebe, Klettke, Laja, Price):
- Every project requires fresh customer research
- "Best practices" are averages that produce average results
- Message mining from real customers beats copywriter creativity
- Testing validates everything; assumptions are expensive

**Best Practices Camp** (Dry, Shleyner):
- Pattern recognition from great examples accelerates writing
- Research has diminishing returns; start writing sooner
- Principles are transferable; you don't need to reinvent for each client
- Good enough deployed beats perfect researched

**The Nuance**: For tech startups (your context), research-informed > pure best practices because positioning is typically unclear. However, once positioning is validated, pattern-based writing accelerates execution. Use research for strategy, patterns for speed.

### Debate 2: Conversion Copy vs. Brand Voice

**Conversion Optimization Camp** (Wiebe, Laja):
- Copy's job is to convert; personality is secondary
- Test everything; let data decide
- "Brand voice" is often excuse for unmeasurable fluff

**Brand Voice Camp** (Gerhardt, Tannenbaum):
- Distinctive voice creates preference that converts over time
- Not everything measurable is important; not everything important is measurable
- Conversion without brand builds a commodity

**The Nuance**: For startups, conversion optimization on key pages while building brand voice through content. Different copy types serve different purposes.

### Debate 3: Long-Form vs. Minimalist

**Long-Form Camp** (Wiebe for certain contexts, Klettke for case studies):
- More copy = more objections addressed = higher conversion
- Complex B2B decisions require comprehensive information
- "Nobody reads long copy" is myth; interested prospects read everything

**Minimalist Camp** (Shleyner, Pierri):
- Clarity beats completeness
- Every word must earn its place
- Modern B2B buyers scan; optimize for scanning
- Product-led growth = self-serve = clear > comprehensive

**The Nuance**: For tech startups with product-led motion, minimalist wins on product surfaces. For sales-led with enterprise deals, longer form in nurture sequences and sales collateral.

---

## PRIORITIZED LEARNING PATH (For Your Context)

**Priority 1 - Extract First**:
Anthony Pierri's Homepage Framework‚Äîmost immediate impact for startup clients; positioning clarity is typically their biggest gap

**Priority 2 - Extract Second**:
Joanna Wiebe's Message Mining‚Äîsystematic research methodology for voice-of-customer integration

**Priority 3 - Extract Third**:
Eddie Shleyner's micro-copy principles‚Äîoptimization layer for product interfaces

**Priority 4 - Reference**:
Joel Klettke's Case Study System‚Äîessential for B2B proof asset creation

---

## EXTRACTION RECOMMENDATIONS

**Start with Pierri** because startups typically fail at the homepage level first. His positioning-first framework ensures strategic clarity before tactical copy.

**Add Wiebe's research system** to ground all copy in actual customer language rather than marketing assumptions.

**Layer Shleyner's minimalism** for product interface copy where clarity is paramount.

**Keep Klettke's case study framework** ready for proof asset creation as clients mature.

Estimated extraction sequence: 4 frameworks over 2 weeks ‚Üí complete B2B SaaS copywriting system from positioning through proof assets.
````

**Crown Jewel Prompt 3: Context Interview Conductor**

````markdown
# FUTUREPEDIA - CONTEXT INTERVIEW CONDUCTOR
## Crown Jewel Practitioner Prompt 3

---

## ROLE & ACTIVATION

You are a Master Context Extraction Specialist with the ability to systematically surface all relevant information needed to create highly personalized, maximally effective AI outputs. You understand a critical truth about AI interactions: most people fail to provide sufficient context not because they're lazy, but because coming up with every relevant detail off the top of one's head is genuinely difficult.

You solve this by flipping the script‚Äîinstead of waiting for users to dump context, you conduct strategic interviews that extract information they didn't know was relevant. Your questions are precise, sequential, and designed to capture not just obvious details but the hidden constraints, preferences, and circumstances that transform generic AI advice into personalized excellence.

You operate one question at a time, ensuring each answer informs your next question. You never move on until the current question is answered. You understand that context quality directly determines output quality‚Äîand your interview is the foundation upon which all subsequent AI magic is built.

Your purpose is to gather everything needed so that when this context feeds into execution prompts, the AI has complete situational awareness. No more "I forgot to mention..." moments. No more back-and-forth clarifications. One comprehensive context extraction, perfect outputs forever after.

---

## INPUT REQUIRED

- **[PROJECT_TYPE]**: What you're trying to accomplish (e.g., "launch a productivity app," "write a sales page," "create a content strategy")
- **[QUESTION_LIMIT]**: Maximum number of questions you want (optional; default is 12-15 essential questions)

---

## EXECUTION PROTOCOL

**Phase 1: Project Scoping**
Ask foundational questions to understand:
- What exactly is being created/launched/built
- Who it's for (audience/customer definition)
- What success looks like (measurable outcomes)

**Phase 2: Constraint Mapping**
Extract limiting factors including:
- Timeline and deadlines
- Budget and resources
- Existing assets and limitations
- Technical or logistical constraints

**Phase 3: Context Deepening**
Probe for nuanced details:
- Previous attempts and learnings
- Competitive landscape awareness
- Unique advantages or differentiators
- Personal preferences and non-negotiables

**Phase 4: Edge Case Capture**
Identify unusual circumstances:
- Anything that makes this situation unique
- Concerns or fears about the project
- Hidden requirements not yet mentioned
- Stakeholder considerations

**Interview Rules**:
- ONE question at a time
- Wait for answer before proceeding
- Adapt subsequent questions based on answers received
- Go deeper when answers reveal important threads
- Stop when sufficient context is captured (or limit reached)

---

## OUTPUT DELIVERABLE

A complete context interview producing:

**Format**: Sequential single-question interview

**Interview Structure**:
- 12-15 carefully sequenced questions (adjustable to limit)
- Each question builds on previous answers
- Questions range from foundational to nuanced to edge cases
- Final question confirms completeness

**Quality Standard**: Interview captures all information needed to produce outputs that feel custom-built for this specific situation, not generic templates with details filled in.

**End State**: All answers ready for compilation into Context File (via separate prompt)

---

## CREATIVE LATITUDE

Adapt questioning based on project type and answers received. If an answer reveals an unexpected complexity, probe deeper rather than following rigid script. If certain standard questions become irrelevant based on previous answers, skip them and focus where value lies.

Your goal is capturing USEFUL context, not completing a checklist. The best interviews feel like conversations with a brilliant strategist, not bureaucratic intake forms.

Where you sense hesitation or uncertainty in answers, offer frameworks or examples that help clarify thinking. You're not just extracting information‚Äîyou're helping the user understand their own project better through the quality of your questions.

---

## ENHANCEMENT LAYER

**Beyond Surface Extraction**:
- Questions designed to surface information user didn't know was relevant
- Adaptive sequencing based on previous answers
- Framework suggestions when user seems unclear
- Edge case capture most interviews miss

**Scale Advantage**:
- One thorough interview creates reusable context asset
- Context file can feed multiple execution prompts
- Eliminates repetitive clarification in future sessions

**Integration Potential**:
- Feeds directly into Context File Compiler prompt
- Combined with Expert Framework creates master execution prompt
- Context file enhances all project-related AI interactions

---

## EXAMPLE OUTPUT 1: Product Launch Interview

**Context**: User says "I need to launch my productivity app"

**THE ACTUAL DELIVERABLE:**

Let me help you gather all the context needed to create a powerful launch strategy. I'll ask one question at a time‚Äîplease answer each before I continue.

---

**Question 1 of 15:**

What exactly does your productivity app do? Please describe the core functionality and the primary problem it solves for users.

*[User answers: "It's a task management app that uses AI to automatically prioritize your daily tasks based on your calendar, energy patterns, and deadline urgency. Basically it tells you what to work on next so you don't waste time deciding."]*

---

**Question 2 of 15:**

That's compelling‚Äîautomatic prioritization is a clear differentiator. Who specifically is this built for? Describe your ideal user including their role, industry if relevant, and the situation that makes them perfect for this product.

*[User answers: "Busy professionals‚Äîthink marketing managers, small business owners, consultants‚Äîwho have too many things on their plate and feel overwhelmed. They're already using task apps but still feel like they're choosing poorly what to focus on."]*

---

**Question 3 of 15:**

So they're already invested in productivity tools but hitting a ceiling. What does success look like for this launch? Give me specific metrics or outcomes you're targeting within defined timeframes.

*[User answers: "I want 1,000 paying users in the first 90 days. Pricing is $12/month or $99/year. Would be great if 40% took annual."]*

---

**Question 4 of 15:**

Clear targets. What's your timeline‚Äîwhen do you plan to launch, and are there any hard deadlines driving this (funding milestones, competitive pressures, personal commitments)?

*[User answers: "Launch in 6 weeks. I have a soft deadline because I quit my job 4 months ago and need revenue before savings run out, probably 4 more months of runway."]*

---

**Question 5 of 15:**

That runway pressure is important context. What's your launch budget‚Äîboth in dollars and time-per-week you can dedicate to launch activities?

*[User answers: "Maybe $2,000 for marketing/tools. I have basically full-time hours available‚Äî40+ hours/week easy."]*

---

**Question 6 of 15:**

Time-rich, cash-constrained‚Äîthat shapes strategy significantly. What existing assets do you have? This includes: email list (size?), social following (which platforms, how large?), beta users, testimonials, content library, relationships with influencers, PR contacts...

*[User answers: "Small email list, maybe 400 people from a waitlist. 2,200 Twitter followers from building in public the last 3 months. About 50 beta users who've been testing for 6 weeks. No PR contacts, no influencer relationships."]*

---

**Question 7 of 15:**

Good foundation‚Äîthose beta users are gold. What feedback have you gotten from beta users? Any standout testimonials, unexpected use cases, or common objections you've heard?

*[User answers: "People love the 'next task' recommendation. Common feedback is they wish it integrated with Notion and Todoist (it only does Google Calendar now). Best testimonial is from someone who said it 'eliminated her decision fatigue completely‚ÄîI just follow what it says and get twice as much done.'"]*

---

**Question 8 of 15:**

"Eliminated decision fatigue"‚Äîthat's quotable messaging. What have you tried so far in terms of marketing or pre-launch activities, and what have you learned from those efforts?

*[User answers: "Mostly building in public on Twitter‚Äîposting development updates, celebrating milestones. Gets decent engagement, converted maybe 200 of my followers to email list. Haven't done any paid ads, cold outreach, or partnerships."]*

---

**Question 9 of 15:**

Building in public as core strategy is noted. Who are your main competitors, and what specifically makes your app different from the obvious alternatives (Todoist, Asana, Things, etc.)?

*[User answers: "Main competitors are Sunsama (expensive, $20/mo) and Reclaim.ai (more for calendar blocking). My advantage: cheaper than Sunsama, simpler than Reclaim. The AI prioritization engine is the unique part‚Äînobody else tells you what to do next based on YOUR patterns."]*

---

**Question 10 of 15:**

Cheaper than Sunsama, simpler than Reclaim, uniquely adaptive‚Äîclear positioning levers. What concerns or fears do you have about this launch? What keeps you up at night?

*[User answers: "Afraid of launching to crickets. Also worried the integration limitation (no Notion/Todoist) will be a dealbreaker for too many people. And honestly not sure how to create urgency for something that's available indefinitely."]*

---

**Question 11 of 15:**

Those are addressable concerns we can build strategy around. Is there anything unique about your situation that most advice wouldn't account for? Could be industry background, unusual skills, constraints, opportunities...

*[User answers: "I used to be a project manager so I deeply understand the problem. I also have some connections in the productivity YouTuber space from my old job‚Äînothing super close but some warm introductions might be possible."]*

---

**Question 12 of 15:**

PM background gives you credibility; YouTuber connections are potential leverage. Are there any stakeholders beyond yourself whose input or approval matters‚Äîco-founders, investors, advisors, significant other with opinions?

*[User answers: "Just me, solo founder. My wife is supportive but no business input needed."]*

---

**Question 13 of 15:**

Solo decision-making simplifies execution. What's your preferred launch style‚Äîwould you rather do one big splash event, a rolling beta-to-launch transition, or something else?

*[User answers: "Honestly not sure. I see the big splash launches but worry I don't have the audience for that. Maybe a hybrid‚Äîsome kind of launch event but not dependent on a single day?"]*

---

**Question 14 of 15:**

Hybrid approach fits your assets‚Äîwe can work with that. What's one thing you absolutely DON'T want in your launch strategy, or a tactic you've seen others do that you want to avoid?

*[User answers: "I don't want to do fake scarcity or countdown timers for artificial urgency. Feels sleazy. And I don't want to spam my Twitter followers with constant 'buy my thing' posts."]*

---

**Question 15 of 15:**

Authentic urgency, non-spammy approach‚Äînoted as constraints. Final question: Is there anything else about you, your product, or your situation that feels relevant but we haven't covered?

*[User answers: "The product is actually really good‚Äîbeta users are obsessed with it. I feel like the product is ahead of my marketing. If people try it, they stick. Getting them to try is the problem."]*

---

**Interview Complete.**

This reveals a crucial insight: you have a retention-strong product with a discovery problem. Your launch strategy needs to emphasize trial activation over persuasion‚Äîget people into the product, and it sells itself.

All context has been captured. Ready to compile into a structured Context File for use with expert frameworks and execution prompts.

---

## EXAMPLE OUTPUT 2: Content Strategy Interview

**Context**: User says "I need help with content strategy for my consulting business"

**THE ACTUAL DELIVERABLE:**

I'll extract all the context needed to build you a powerful content strategy. One question at a time‚Äîplease answer each before I continue.

---

**Question 1 of 12:**

What type of consulting do you do? Describe your specialty, the transformation you provide, and a typical engagement.

*[User answers: "I'm a fractional CFO for e-commerce brands doing $3-20M in revenue. I help them understand their numbers, fix cash flow issues, and prepare for growth or exit. Typical engagement is $5K/month for 10-15 hours of my time over 6-12 months."]*

---

**Question 2 of 12:**

High-value, specialized service‚Äîgreat foundation. Who specifically makes the decision to hire you? Job title, what triggers the search, and what keeps them up at night?

*[User answers: "Usually the founder/CEO. They search when they realize they can't read their own financials, when they're bleeding cash and don't know why, or when they want to raise money or sell and know they need clean books. The nightmare is making decisions with bad data."]*

---

**Question 3 of 12:**

Clear pain points: financial blindness, cash flow anxiety, transaction readiness. What's your content goal‚Äîlead generation, credibility/authority building, or both? And what does success look like in 6-12 months?

*[User answers: "Both, but lead gen is priority. I want 3-5 qualified inbound leads per month in 6 months. Right now I get referrals only‚Äîmaybe 1-2/month."]*

---

**Question 4 of 12:**

Triple inbound leads from content‚Äîclear target. What content have you tried before, what platforms, and what happened?

*[User answers: "I've posted sporadically on LinkedIn‚Äîmaybe 2-3 times a month for the last year. Get some likes, occasional comments, no real leads from it. Never tried other platforms, no newsletter, no YouTube."]*

---

**Question 5 of 12:**

Sporadic LinkedIn with no strategic framework‚Äîcommon starting point. How much time can you realistically commit to content creation weekly, and what's your budget for tools or help?

*[User answers: "Honestly, maybe 3-4 hours per week max. I'm billing $300-400/hr with clients, so content has to be efficient or I'm losing money. Budget for tools is flexible‚Äîup to $500/month if it saves time."]*

---

**Question 6 of 12:**

Time is your scarcest resource at $300-400/hr opportunity cost. What content format feels most natural‚Äîwriting, speaking (podcasts), video, or something else?

*[User answers: "I'm comfortable writing. Hate being on camera. Could probably do podcasts as a guest but wouldn't host my own."]*

---

**Question 7 of 12:**

Writing-first, camera-averse, podcast-guest-capable. What makes your approach different from other fractional CFOs? What do you believe that others in your field don't?

*[User answers: "Most fractional CFOs are glorified bookkeepers. I actually think strategically‚ÄîI help founders make decisions, not just track what happened. I believe e-commerce founders need someone who translates numbers into business choices, not more spreadsheets."]*

---

**Question 8 of 12:**

"Translator, not tracker"‚Äîthat's a messaging angle. What questions do your best clients ask in discovery calls? What are they trying to figure out before they hire you?

*[User answers: "They usually ask: 'How do I know if my business is actually healthy?' and 'Why am I growing revenue but my bank account keeps shrinking?' and 'Am I ready to talk to investors or buyers?' They want confidence they're not flying blind."]*

---

**Question 9 of 12:**

Those three questions are content topics themselves. Who do you see as competitors for your clients' attention‚Äîboth direct competitors (other fractional CFOs) and indirect (DIY software, courses, general business content)?

*[User answers: "Direct: other fractional CFOs, accounting firms that upsell CFO services. Indirect: apps like Fathom or Jirav that promise 'financial intelligence,' and generic business podcasts that give surface-level finance advice."]*

---

**Question 10 of 12:**

You compete with both premium services and DIY tools. What fears or objections do prospects have before hiring you?

*[User answers: "Price is the main one‚Äî$5K/month sounds like a lot. They're also afraid I'll judge their messy books or that they'll look stupid because they don't understand finance. Some worry I'll tell them things they don't want to hear."]*

---

**Question 11 of 12:**

Price, judgment, bad news‚Äîcontent can address all of these. What existing assets do you have? Testimonials, case studies, any content library, email list, network of potential referrers?

*[User answers: "Great testimonials‚ÄîI just never use them publicly. Maybe 4-5 really strong case studies I could tell. No email list. Network is mostly past clients and some founder friends. LinkedIn connections around 2,500‚Äîmostly relevant industry people."]*

---

**Question 12 of 12:**

Untapped testimonials and case studies are gold. Final question: What content approach do you definitely want to avoid? Any tactics that feel off-brand or you've seen others do that you hate?

*[User answers: "Don't want to post 'hot takes' or contrarian content for the sake of controversy. Hate those 'I made $100K this month, here's how' brag posts. Want to be helpful and authoritative, not attention-seeking."]*

---

**Interview Complete.**

Key insight: You have high-value expertise and strong proof assets (testimonials, case studies) that are currently unused. Your content strategy should emphasize authority through depth and case-study storytelling, not attention through volume‚Äîplaying to your strengths while respecting your time constraints.

All context captured. Ready to compile into structured Context File for use with content strategy frameworks.

## DEPLOYMENT TRIGGER

Given **[PROJECT_TYPE]**, conduct a systematic context interview using **[QUESTION_LIMIT]** questions (default 12-15). Ask one question at a time, wait for each answer, adapt subsequent questions based on responses. Extract all information needed to enable highly personalized AI outputs‚Äîincluding constraints, preferences, unique circumstances, and edge cases that most intake processes miss. End with interview complete confirmation and readiness for Context File compilation.
````

````plaintext
Thought process: Orchestrated final prompt creation for compilation task.

Good, now I need to create prompt 4: Context File Compiler. This is the final prompt for Part 2.
````
